<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This paper unfolds the recent concept of using harmonic signals generated by the nonlinear behavior of traditional passive UHF RF identification (RFID) chips. The harmonics generation of passive RFID chips is analyzed to highlight the influences of the matching network and the tag antenna. The proposed study relies on a theoretical model that explains the role in the harmonic production of different elements constituting the tag. The model also shows how to achieve a second communication channel exploiting the third harmonic frequency in addition to the fundamental frequency channel. Specifications and methodology are explained in a harmonic communication scenario. The regulations, harmonic RFID reader considerations, harmonic tag guidelines design, and metrics for its evaluation are discussed. In compliance with the standard regulations EPC Class-1 Gen2 RFID, a design example is presented. The performance of the solution is illustrated from simulation and measurements. The prototype example operates simultaneously at fundamental and third harmonic frequencies with a read range greater than 4.5 m.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.purpose -->

<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>RF identification (RFID) is a wireless data-collection technology very popular in many applications and services such as logistics, manufacturing, and security <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. Today, the scope of the passive RFID technology is not limited to identification, but has a variety of new applications in the sensing of environment and human body parameters <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, tag-to-tag communication <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, or redundant backscattering modulation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. Moreover, RFID is leading the new paradigm of Internet of Things (IoT) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>.</p><p>Passive UHF RFID tags are composed by one antenna loaded by an RFID chip. One of the duties performed by the RFID chip is the energy scavenging by RF rectification. The rectifier converts the RF carrier wave sent by the reader to a direct current (dc), thus allowing the chip to power its circuitry and operate as a transponder. The architecture of the rectifier is based on a Dickson topology <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a> with two or more diode-based voltage doubler stages that determines the nonlinear behavior of the RFID chip.</p><p>The main objective of this paper is to perform an in-depth study of the nonlinear behavior of the rectifier part and to demonstrate that the nonlinearities could be exploited, and thus open the door to several new applications in passive UHF RFID systems.</p><p>The study and the exploitation of the nonlinearity in diode-based devices are not new. Approaches based on a 1-bit system in which the harmonic or intermodulation signals serve to indicate the presence of the tag without any specific communication protocol are known as the harmonic radar. Used as a tracking solution, the harmonic radar invention was patented in 1975 <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, paving the way for several derived applications, e.g., in insect tracking <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>. With the boom of RFID systems, the harmonic radar concept has been recently re-proposed. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>, a tag response is achieved by exploiting the intermodulation phenomenon of a diode. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a>, a specific nonlinear RF circuit is developed with the aim of enhancing the harmonic strength compared to multiplier diodes used at 10 GHz, afterwards the circuit integrated to an antenna is used in accurate indoor ranging <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a>. Rasilainen et al. <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_1">[16]</a> have studied and generalized the design techniques for harmonic transponders based on a single detector or varactor diode. The concept was adopted for low-cost solutions using paper substrates and inkjet printing technology <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_1">[17]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_1">[18]</a> or even an eco-friendly solution using an organic diode <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_1">[19]</a>. Another exploitation idea <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_1">[20]</a> proposes the detection of counterfeit RFID cards based on its electromagnetic characteristics rather than the digital information that they transmit. In this approach, one of the stages considers the electromagnetic signature that harmonic signals produce. An emerging field in where the nonlinearity of diode-based devices is also being exploited is the electromagnetic energy harvesting. Trotter et al. <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_1">[21]</a>, Collado and Georgiadis <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_1">[22]</a>, Boaventura et al. <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_1">[23]</a>, and Borges Carvalho et al. <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_1">[24]</a> have proposed power-optimized waveforms to improve the range and reliability of RFID systems. By using special designed signal waveforms at the transmitting terminal that somehow excite the diode nonlinear behavior in a more efficient manner triggering in an increased RF-to-dc conversion efficiency. In the same field, the work reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref25" id="context_ref_25_1">[25]</a> proposes a millimeter-wave rectenna at 35 GHz that harvests the harmonic signals generated by its rectifier, also enhancing the total RF-to-dc conversion efficiency.</p><p>In the specific field of passive UHF RFID EPC Class 1 Gen2, the experimentation with backscattered harmonics has been first introduced in 2009 <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_1">[26]</a>, but no additional research efforts were followed, probably because of the evidenced low power and limitations on the characterization method. Recently, the authors of this paper have presented characterization platforms and results proving the harmonic backscattering feasibility <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_1">[27]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_1">[28]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_1">[29]</a>.</p><p>Contrary to the conventional paradigm in RF communication circuits where nonlinearities are undesired and their level is highly reduced <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_1">[30]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref31" id="context_ref_31_1">[31]</a>, this paper develops the concept of a new communication function by exploiting nonlinearities of passive EPC Class-1 Gen2 RFID chips. The exploitation of harmonic signals as information carriers establishes frequency diversity from tag to reader, without breaches to standard regulations. The benefit of the frequency diversity is the possibility to use a spectrum, which has much reduced self- and multi-path interference, therefore countering multi-path and leakage effects at reception. With such a motivation, this paper aims to meet the following three specific objectives.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>To perform a theoretical analysis of harmonic signals produced by the RF section of passive RFID tags. The analysis pinpoints in the operation of a traditional tag working at the fundamental frequency of the system (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-4" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), but also to enhance the backscattered signal strength at its third harmonic <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-8" role="math" style="width: 2.405em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.165em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.04em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-11" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">(3f_{0})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, hereinafter the so-called harmonic tag (HT) (<a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>).</p></li><li><p>To define exploitation policies when the harmonic communication HT reader is envisaged. The policies treat regulation definitions, considerations on the reader side, metrics to evaluate the HT performance, and design guidelines for the HT (<a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>).</p></li><li><p>To explain the HT design and operation with a real HT design example and an in-depth parametric study in terms of power, frequency, and read range performance (<a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>).</p></li></ul>The developed concept could establish a foundation for new potential applications that the redundant information carried by the chip self-generated harmonics could offer. The final conclusion and perspectives of the approach are drawn in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a>.<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Theoretical Considerations: Harmonic Produced By Passive RFID Chips and Effects of The Antenna</h2></div><p>This section explains the harmonic production of passive RFID chips and afterwards the effects produced by the matching network and the tag antenna on the harmonic backscattering phenomena. The theoretical analysis is developed in the following three stages.
</p><ul style="list-style-type: none;"><li><p>The calculation of a general expression for the current in the rectifier part of the RFID chip. The expression comprises fundamental and harmonic components.</p></li><li><p>The study of the matching network used in traditional RFID tags in order to evaluate the harmonic backscattering strength.</p></li><li><p>The study of a new matching network architecture that enhances the backscattering strength at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-18" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.38em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-19"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-20" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-21"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-22" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-23"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-25" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> maintaining the operation at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-26" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-27"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-28"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-29" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-30"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-31"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-32" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, therefore constituting the HT operation theory.</p></li></ul>The analysis presented in this section uses an equivalent circuit (based on lumped components) to model the operation of the distributed impedance matching network integrated in traditional RFID tag antennas. The model is not a generalization of a special case, but explains the typical impedance matching between a chip and a dipole-based antenna at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-33" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-34"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-35"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-36" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-37"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-38"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-39" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Additionally the model shows how to achieve a second communication channel exploiting the harmonic generated by the chip at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-40" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.38em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-41"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-42" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-43"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-44" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-45"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-46"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-47" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. Analysis of Harmonic Currents in the Rectifier</h3><div class="section_2" id="sec2a1"><h4>1. Review of Dickson Analysis</h4><p>The most extended architecture used to study the rectification process in UHF RFID is the Dickson charge pump and its derived equations <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_2a1">[7]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref32" id="context_ref_32_2a1">[32]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_2a1">[33]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref34" id="context_ref_34_2a1">[34]</a>. Although the rectifier architecture used in this paper is very similar to the Dickson charge pump, it has some significative differences <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2a1">[8]</a>. Since UHF tags operate with significantly lower signal levels and higher frequency than the original Dickson analysis, some modifications must be made to the RF-to-dc equation proposed by Dickson. The original Dickson analysis assumes constant forward voltage drop of the rectification device, so-called “threshold voltage,” though this forward voltage drop is actually a function of the load current of the rectifier. This variation is not significant for large voltage swings across the diode as is the case for the charge pump application. However in passive UHF RFID, the RF input voltage is very small, on the same order of the forward voltage drop. As a result, the nonlinear forward voltage drop has significant impact on the RF-to-dc equation. In this context, a parametric nonlinear analysis theory has been developed to incorporate the effect of the nonlinear forward voltage drop. The analysis was first applied to predict the RF-to-dc conversion for single-diode rectifiers in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref35" id="context_ref_35_2a1">[35]</a> and was later expanded to multi-stage rectifiers in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_2a1">[30]</a>.</p><p>Being aware of the low RF input voltage present in UHF RFID applications, the multi-stage voltage multiplier model and the analysis method used in this paper is supported by several works that use similar architectures to predict the RF-to-dc conversion of rectifiers in passive UHF RFID <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_2a1">[30]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref36" id="context_ref_36_2a1">[36]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref37" id="context_ref_37_2a1">[37]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref38" id="context_ref_38_2a1">[38]</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a> shows the RF section of a passive RFID tag, having a two-stage voltage multiplier, hereinafter referenced as the rectifier. The rectifier circuitry can be composed by a cascade of an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-48" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.84em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-49"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-50" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-stage voltage multiplier.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Passive RFID tag architecture.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Due to the nonlinear effects of the rectifier part of the RFID chip, the current in the antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-51" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-52"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-53"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-54" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">I<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; Indeed, in the scavenging state (i.e., state of modulation when maximum power is transmitted to the chip), the input voltage induced in the tag antenna, and then, conducted to the rectifier at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-60" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; It should be noted that this model does not consider the parasitic effects of the package.</p><p>Since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-209" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.413em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.421em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">(V_{0}=0.15\ {\hbox{V}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1255" role="math" style="width: 1.524em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.194em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001.19em 2.583em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1256"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1257"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.194em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1000.53em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1258" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">I<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.194em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001.19em 2.583em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1263"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1264"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.194em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1000.53em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1265" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">I<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.069em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.466em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1266"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1267"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1268" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">10</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.254em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-85">I_{10}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and it becomes closer as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1269" role="math" style="width: 1.26em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.995em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001em 2.583em -999.997em); clip: rect(3.112em 1000.8em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1272" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">V<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.202em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.599em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1273"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1274"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1275" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.254em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">V_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. Third Harmonic in Traditional Tags</h3><div class="section_2" id="sec2b1"><h4>1. Impedance Matching Network for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1276" role="math" style="width: 1.027em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.899em; height: 0px; font-size: 112%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.219em 1000.9em 2.499em -999.997em); top: -2.109em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1277"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1278"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.899em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.075em 1000.58em 4.355em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1279" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.067em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.971em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.837em; left: 0.515em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1280"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1281"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1282" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.971em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.115em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.283em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.151em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h4><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a> shows the model of the matching network used in passive RFID tags. The model is not a generalization of a special case, but actually it is based on three real features of passive RFID chips: 1) the input impedance is always capacitive at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1283" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1284"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1285"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1286" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1287"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1288"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1289" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> because of its diode-based rectifier circuit <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_2b1">[30]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref31" id="context_ref_31_2b1">[31]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref38" id="context_ref_38_2b1">[38]</a>; 2) the impedance is represented by the parallel configuration of a capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1290" role="math" style="width: 1.685em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.5em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1291"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1292"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1293" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1294"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1295"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1296" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1297" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">q<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">C_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and a resistance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1298" role="math" style="width: 1.685em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.5em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1299"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1300"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1301" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1302"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1303"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1304" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1305" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">q<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-90">R_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> because it fits best the RFID chip impedance in a wide frequency band <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref40" id="context_ref_40_2b1">[40]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref41" id="context_ref_41_2b1">[41]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref42" id="context_ref_42_2b1">[42]</a>; and 3) the impedance is matched to the one of a dipole-based antenna (around 73 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1306" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1307"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1308" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-91">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and zero imaginary component at the resonant frequency) to form the RFID tag.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Equivalent circuit of the RF section of a passive RFID tag.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Given the capacitive nature of RFID chips, an impedance-matching network is always introduced between the RFID chip and a resistive dipole antenna. The operation of the matching network is as follows: the first element is the shunt inductance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1309" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1000.96em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1310"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1311"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1312" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1313"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1314"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1315" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">′</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-92">L^{\prime}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> that compensates <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-93-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1316" role="math" style="width: 1.685em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.5em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1317"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1318"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1319" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1320"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1321"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1322" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1323" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">q<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-93">C_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and represents the traditional inductive loop used in RFID antenna design <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref42" id="context_ref_42_2b1">[42]</a> (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-94-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1324" role="math" style="width: 1.685em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.5em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1325"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1326"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1327" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1328"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1329"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1330" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1331" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">q<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-94">C_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> describes the capacitive nature of the RFID chip). Once the chip reactance is canceled, the remaining high shunt resistance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1332" role="math" style="width: 1.685em; padding-left: 0.303em;">1.8</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1523" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1524"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1525"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1526"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1527"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1528" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">k</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1529" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-119">R_{\rm eq}=1.8\ {\hbox{k}}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> constant. The higher the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-120-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1530" role="math" style="width: 0.904em; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-120">Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the better the power matching is, or in other words, greater isolation at frequencies different than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-121-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1533" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1534"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1535"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1536" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1537"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1538"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1539" style="font-size: 70.7%; MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-126-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-126">Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula> on the signal radiated by traditional tag antennas at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-127-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-127">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is modeled using the architecture depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm ant}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-128-Frame" The input power to the matching network is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ant}=V_{\rm ant}I_{\rm ant}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-133-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-133">P_{\rm ant}=V_{\rm ant}I_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the output power of the matching network is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm eq}=V_{\rm in}I_{\rm in}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-134-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-134">P_{\rm eq}=V_{\rm in}I_{\rm in}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm ant}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-135-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Equivalent circuit of the tag when the current at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-139-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-139">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is being reflected in the antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
From <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8" href="#deqn8" class="fulltext-link">(8)</a>, the amplitude of the current in the antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm 1ant}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-140-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-140">I_{\rm 1ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-141-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-141">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is given by <disp-formula id="deqn9" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\left\vert I_{\rm 1ant}\right\vert=I_{10}\sqrt{Q^{2}+1}\eqno{\hbox{(9)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-142-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; In order to find a similar relation between <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm 3in}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-146-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-146">I_{\rm 3in}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the component of the rectifier input current at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-147-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-147">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm 3ant}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-148-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-148">I_{\rm 3ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the reflected current in the antenna terminals at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-149-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-149">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, an equivalent model of the tag backscattering the harmonic is presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>. Let <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{3}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-150-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-150">V_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> be the shunt voltage when the current <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span 3in}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>, and therefore <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{3}=I_{\rm 3in}Z_{\rm 3in}</span><span class="MathJax <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm 3in}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-154-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script Replacing the relations between <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C,L,R_{A},R_{\rm eq},</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" possible to calculate the amplitude of the current in the antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">I_{\rm 3ant}</span><span class="MathJax From the capacitive nature of the RFID chip, the resistance conversion of the matching network from a high shunt resistance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-171-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-171">R_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (around 1.8 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{k}}\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-172-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-172">{\hbox{k}}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), to a comparatively lower series resistance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{A}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-173-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-173">R_{A}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (around 73 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-174-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-174">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), imposes that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C\gg C_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-175-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-175">C\gg C_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L^{\prime}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-176-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-176">L^{\prime}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> resonates with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-177-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-177">C_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-178-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-178">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, then <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">L^{\prime}=1/C_{\rm eq}\omega_{0}^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-179-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-179">L^{\prime}=1/C_{\rm eq}\omega_{0}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The following statement, in agreement with <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_2b2">[30]</a>, is then derived: <disp-formula id="deqn12" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q\omega_{0}L^{\prime}\gg R_{\rm eq}.\eqno{\hbox{(12)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-180-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; From <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn9" href="#deqn9" class="fulltext-link">(9)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn13" href="#deqn13" class="fulltext-link">(13)</a>, it is possible to calculate the power delivered to the tag antenna terminals at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing"
