<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm 1HT}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-275-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-275">P_{\rm 1HT}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-276-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-276">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, in function of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q^{\ast}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-277-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-277">Q^{\ast}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-278-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-278">Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the ratio <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{0}/V_{t}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-279-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-279">V_{0}/V_{t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. If the matching network is well designed, which means an antenna having a distributed matching network that cancels the RFID chip reactance at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-280-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-280">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-281-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-281">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the difference between the backscattered power by the HT at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-282-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-282">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-283-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-283">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> depends only on the intrinsic nonlinear behavior of the chip (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>) and is represented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11(b)</a> at a certain level of input voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-284-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-284">V_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>Law decay of the power at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-285-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-285">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with respect to the power at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-286-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-286">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the HT. (a) In function of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q^{\ast}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-287-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-287">Q^{\ast}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-288-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-288">Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-289-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-289">V_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (b) In function of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-290-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-290">V_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. If the matching network is well dimensioned, the ratio depends only on the nonlinearity of the chip.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Conducted measurement tests based on emulating proper matching networks at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-291-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-291">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> were reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_2c2">[29]</a>. The tests, so-called harmonic treatments, shows an enhancement of 11 dB in the chip response at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-292-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-292">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with respect to the case of an optimum emulated antenna at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-293-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-293">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with the same chip. These results, in agreement with the theory above exposed, show the importance of the matching network in the harmonic exploitation at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-294-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-294">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></div></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>RFID Harmonic Communication: Specifications and Methodology</h2></div><p>The theoretical analysis has shown the possibility to increase the backscattering strength at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-295-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-295">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by exploiting the harmonic generation of passive RFID chips. This section aims to present considerations on the use of HTs in a tag-to-reader harmonic communication regard. Indeed it is intended to declare the diversity in frequency where signals from tag-to-reader at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-296-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-296">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-297-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-297">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> carry the same information. Aspects such as deployment regulations, harmonic reader operation considerations, HT evaluation metrics, and HT design guidelines are unfolded.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Compliance With Regulations</h3><div class="section_2" id="sec3a1"><h4>1. Regulations At <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-298-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-298">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h4><p>In order to not create obstacles or delays in the use of the HT, e.g., regarding the compatibility with other systems, the parent design policy is to respect current standards and local regulations that control the passive UHF RFID system operation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref46" id="context_ref_46_3a1">[46]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref47" id="context_ref_47_3a1">[47]</a>. In that regard, since dual-band operation is desired (at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-299-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-299">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from the passive UHF RFID system, i.e., in Europe, 868 MHz, and at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-300-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-300">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, i.e., 2604 MHz), reader and tag spectrum regulatory masks must be respected.</p><p>No particular change is envisaged on the transmitter side of the RFID reader, in other words, HTs should operate with RFID readers that meet the regulations <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref46" id="context_ref_46_3a1">[46]</a>. In the same manner, the tag spectrum mask defined in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref47" id="context_ref_47_3a1">[47]</a> should be respected. The first sidelobe of the tag response signal shall not exceed −20 dBm of effective radiated power (ERP) at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-301-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-301">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. All other spurious signals like its harmonics must not exceed these limits.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3a2"><h4>2. Regulations At 3<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-302-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-302">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h4><p>In Europe, the spectrum regulations allocate the frequency band of 2500–2690 MHz to broadband mobile services (e.g., long-term evolution (LTE) and WIMAX with transmitters of tens of watts and operation distances up to 4 km) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref48" id="context_ref_48_3a2">[48]</a>. In other regions (e.g., where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}=2745\ {\hbox{MHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-303-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-303">3f_{0}=2745\ {\hbox{MHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), the band of 2700–2900 MHz is worldwide allocated to meteorological and air traffic radar systems with high power (the equivalent isotropically radiated power could be on the order of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{10}}^{9}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-304-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-304">{\hbox{10}}^{9}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> W) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref48" id="context_ref_48_3a2">[48]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref49" id="context_ref_49_3a2">[49]</a>. Studies, based on worst case assumptions (i.e., line-of-sight conditions), have shown that there is potential interference from mobile service to radar and vice versa, which will depend on the deployment scenario with factors such as frequency separation, relative antenna orientation, and distance (in the order of several kilometers), but nevertheless the systems are still compatible <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref48" id="context_ref_48_3a2">[48]</a>.</p><p>Given the backscattering modulation nature of passive UHF RFID systems, even if the tag response at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-305-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-305">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is enhanced for the harmonic communication approach, it remains weak (the equivalent isotropically radiated power could be on the order of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{10}}^{-11}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-306-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-306">{\hbox{10}}^{-11}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> W at a few meters) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_3a2">[28]</a>, and does not represent an incompatibility issue compared to the possible radar effects on the mobile service. If reader and tag regulatory masks are respected, the operation at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-307-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-307">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> will ensure the regulatory compliances.</p></div></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Harmonic Reader Considerations</h3><p>In a communication scenario reader-HTs, some considerations in the dimensioning of the harmonic branch receiver of an RFID harmonic reader should be taken into account. Specific details in the baseband treatment and the analog-to-digital conversion are out of the scope of this work, and could be taken as a future line of research. However, certain directives regarding the harmonic RFID reader operation can be stated. A critical issue in the design of traditional RFID readers (i.e., working at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-308-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-308">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) is the suppression of the carrier wave signal that unintentionally leaks into the received path due to the use of common isolation techniques as circulator or couplers. The reader has to transmit a strong carrier wave signal to supply passive tags with sufficient operating power. The response of the tag, on the other hand, is generated by passive backscattering, which is achieved by a modulation of the RFID chip input impedance. Since only a small fraction of the power incident upon the tag is reradiated, the signal received by the interrogator antenna is very weak compared to the transmitted carrier wave signal <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref50" id="context_ref_50_3b">[50]</a>. Therefore, the reduction of the transmitted leak is crucial and leads traditional reader architectures to increase the reception sensitivity of RFID readers <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref50" id="context_ref_50_3b">[50]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref51" id="context_ref_51_3b">[51]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref52" id="context_ref_52_3b">[52]</a>.</p><p>From measurement results in passive UHF RFID <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_3b">[27]</a>, the carrier wave at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-309-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-309">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is around 60 dB below the carrier wave at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-310-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-310">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. By using harmonic backscattering, in case of a receiver at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-311-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-311">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the limitations imposed by the carrier wave leakage does not represent a great inconvenience. Indeed, the conditions are favorable to design a receiver with higher sensitivity than the achieved one at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-312-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-312">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Some noise may result from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-313-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-313">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> leakage due to the synchronization circuitry at reception, but it is much smaller than the circulator or coupler leakage at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-314-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-314">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_3b">[14]</a>. As in traditional passive RFID, the overall system performance in the harmonic communication scenario is limited by the tag. Thus, a proper HT antenna that allows the harmonic produced by the chip at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-315-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-315">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to be backscattered will collaborate to the harmonic reader dimensioning by reducing its sensitivity requirements, in other words, increasing the read range of the HT.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3c"><h3>C. HT Antenna Basics</h3><p>With the intention to integrate the antenna-chip matching network directly in the antenna structure or to reduce the size of the antennas, plenty of documentation on RFID antenna design exists <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref42" id="context_ref_42_3c">[42]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref53" id="context_ref_53_3c">[53]</a>. In the case of the HT, the main difference respect to traditional tag antennas is the dual-band operation. As exposed in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2c" class="fulltext-link">Section II-C</a>, the HT should include a distributed matching network that cancels the RFID chip reactance at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-316-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-316">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-317-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-317">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Depending on the required application, some antenna parameters can be optimized with respect to others (size, directivity, materials, etc.).</p><p>The HT design process is illustrated in a flowchart shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a>. As in traditional RFID <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref53" id="context_ref_53_3c">[53]</a>, the design requirements are linked to the required application (size, directivity, read range, operation conditions, materials of the tagged object, etc.).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12. </b><fig><p>RFID ht antenna design process.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Having fixed the material, the design of an HT antenna begins by importing the scattering parameters of the chips in a scavenging state into a electromagnetic simulator <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_3c">[29]</a>. Given that the impedance of the RFID chip at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-318-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-318">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is still capacitive <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_3c">[29]</a>, inductively loop matching techniques used at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-319-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-319">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can still be used at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-320-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-320">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Generalizing, the inductive compensation of antennas loaded with capacitive diode-based circuits such as RFID chips or rectifier circuits is valid for the HT antenna. Therefore, antenna design techniques used for dual-band rectennas or harmonic radar can be applied to the design of the HT antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_3c">[15]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3c">[16]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref54" id="context_ref_54_3c">[54]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref55" id="context_ref_55_3c">[55]</a>. Under this criterion, the chosen antenna should include two inductive loops, each of them to compensate the capacitive impedance of the chip at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-321-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-321">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-322-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-322">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The simulation is led to optimize the antenna structure based on the design requirements (impedance matching, antenna gain, read range, de-tuning effects). Starting with the impedance matching at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-323-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-323">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and after at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-324-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-324">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, certain changes on the dimensions of elements that cause the resonance at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-325-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-325">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> could be necessary, nevertheless the optimization process facilitates the procedure once the structure operation is mastered. Finally, some prototypes should be fabricated and tested in order to validate the design requirements.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3d"><h3>D. Setup and Metrics To Evaluate Harmonic RFID Tags</h3><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 13. </b><fig><p>(a) Equipment setup used for bi-static configuration. (b) Bi-static configuration in the anechoic chamber.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
The evaluation of the HT performance is based on radiated measurements performed in a confined environment. Similar test setups to those ones used for traditional passive RFID can be used <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref56" id="context_ref_56_3d">[56]</a>, but certain considerations on the analysis methods should be taken, i.e., the analysis proposed in this section quantifies the HT response by measuring the power spectral density (PSD) of the signal at the frequency of interest. A calibrated power budget is necessary to perform accurate measurements of the HT response at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-326-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-326">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-327-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-327">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Specific details concerning the used methodology and the RFID air interface settings can be found in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_3d">[27]</a>.<p></p><p>The evaluation tests reported in this paper use the measurement setup shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13</a>. An anechoic chamber with bi-static configuration (1-m distance between horn antennas and tag) is connected to the RFID test-platform (RFID-TP). The RFID-TP performs a PSD analysis in real time at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-328-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-328">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-329-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-329">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Regarding the power budget and measurements, the results reported consider the following guidelines.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>HT sensitivity at different frequencies. The necessary ERP power (i.e., transmitted power before the antenna) sent by the RFID-TP to activate the HT is considered. The ERP power is calculated using the power approach defined in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref57" id="context_ref_57_3d">[57]</a>. Since the measurement setup is completely calibrated and controlled, the ERP is known. This consideration allows the evaluation of the HT performance independently of the kind of reader antenna used.</p></li><li><p>HT response at different RFID-TP power levels. The HT response is evaluated in terms of the isotropic received power (values calibrated to a receiving antenna of 0-dBi gain) in function of the equivalent isotropic radiated power (EIRP) transmitted by the RFID-TP. Furthermore, in the measure of the HT response, the PSD analysis considers the power contained in both first sidelobes of the modulated response, contrary to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref58" id="context_ref_58_3d">[58]</a>, where only one sidelobe is considered. It is worth noting that the harmonic response exists conditioned to the existence of the response at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-330-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-330">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></li><li><p>HT read range performance. The read range is calculated using the law of decay <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">20{\rm log}(d)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-331-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-331">20{\rm log}(d)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-332-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-332">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the distance between the tag and reader beyond 1 m, being known as the tag response at 1 m, and considering a radiated level of 35-dBm EIRP for the RFID-TP <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref59" id="context_ref_59_3d">[59]</a>. Therefore, the calculation of the HT response at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-333-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-333">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-334-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-334">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> beyond 1 m is possible and it is compatible with the methods used in the literature <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref53" id="context_ref_53_3d">[53]</a>. For the read range evaluation, a 6-dBi antenna gain is considered for the EIRP of the RFID-TP. This analysis allows to represent the read range for a given sensitivity of the reader receiver at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-335-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-335">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-336-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-336">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></li></ul><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>HT Design Example</h2></div><p>This section attempts to illustrate the exposed theory of the HT by presenting a design example. Later on, an in-depth parametric study in terms of frequency, power, and read range describes the operation of the realized prototype.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. HT Design</h3><div class="section_2" id="sec4a1"><h4>1. Design Requirements</h4><p>The requirements for the HT in this example are: 1) a maximum read range at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}=868\ {\hbox{MHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-337-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-337">f_{0}=868\ {\hbox{MHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}=2604\ {\hbox{MHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-338-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-338">3f_{0}=2604\ {\hbox{MHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>; 2) antenna size and flexibility comparable to the ones of existing RFID inlays; and 3) the use of low-cost materials and prototype techniques. Regarding the impedance at both bands, the design example uses the chip GX2L NXP SOT1040-AA1 <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref40" id="context_ref_40_4a1">[40]</a> with measured impedances <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">19-j178\ \Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-339-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-339">19-j178\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-340-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-340">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">9.2-j54.2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-341-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-341">9.2-j54.2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-342-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-342">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-343-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-343">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_4a1">[29]</a>. In agreement with the requirements, the chosen materials are PET with 3.2 permittivity and 0.05-mm thickness for the substrate and aluminum as trace conductor. The next step is to choose an antenna structure in where the double inductive loop matching technique can be applied.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4a2"><h4>2. Antenna Structure</h4><p>A Yagi–Uda structure used in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref55" id="context_ref_55_4a2">[55]</a> for a dual-band rectenna and modified in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4a2">[28]</a> to include the double inductive loop is chosen as structure of reference for this example. The modified Yagi–Uda structure complies with the initial requirements of dual-band operation, comparable size to traditional inlays, and possibility to be printed on a thin, flexible, and low-cost substrate. The presented example incorporates a new director element to the structure used in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4a2">[28]</a> aiming to increase the directivity at the harmonic frequency. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a> shows the HT structure composed by four main parts.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>Fundamental resonator: the resonant structure at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-344-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-344">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is a curved dipole conforming a loop [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14(b)</a>] in order to achieve the conjugate chip impedance matching at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-345-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-345">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref42" id="context_ref_42_4a2">[42]</a>.</p></li><li><p>Harmonic resonator: the resonant structure at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-346-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-346">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is a dipole joint to an inductive loop [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14(a)</a>] in order to achieve the conjugate chip impedance matching at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-347-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-347">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></li><li><p>Reflector: a reflector at the rear of the antenna [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14(c)</a>] serves to increase the directivity at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-348-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-348">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>; its position and dimensions also allow to tune the resistance of the antenna.</p></li><li><p>Director: a director at the front of the antenna [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14(d)</a>] serves also to increase the directivity at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-349-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-349">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></li></ul>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 14. </b><fig><p>HT prototype. (a) Harmonic resonator. (b) Fundamental resonator. (c) Reflector. (d) Director.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Regarding the feeding point, the harmonic resonator and the fundamental resonator are joined by two parallel lines, where, in each line, one port of the chip is connected.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4a3"><h4>3. Simulation Results</h4><p>A parametric simulation and optimization is performed where the goal is to maximize the read range at both frequencies (the optimization goal is to have a minimum reflection coefficient at both bands). Starting with an impedance matching at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-350-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-350">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (trimming the fundamental resonator and fundamental inductive loop), and then looking for the matching at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-351-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-351">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (trimming the harmonic resonator and harmonic inductive loop). The dimensions of both resonators, both inductive loops, reflector, and director are finally tuned by optimization.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 15</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">16</a> show the copolarized directivity of the designed antenna in plane <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E(xy)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-352-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-352">E(xy)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and plane <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">H(zy)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-353-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-353">H(zy)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively. Directivity results are compared to those of the antenna without the director reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4a3">[28]</a> for each plane. A hybrid directivity is conformed by the following.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>A quasi-omnidirectional pattern at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-354-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-354">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>: i.e., the realized directivity at 868 MHz is 2.18 dBi, being close to the 2.5 dBi reported in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4a3">[28]</a>.</p></li><li><p>A directive pattern at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-355-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-355">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>: i.e., the realized directivity at 2604 MHz is 6.31 dBi, higher than the 3 dBi reported in the literature <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4a3">[28]</a>.</p></li></ul>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 15. </b><fig><p>Simulated directivity in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-356-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-356">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane for the modified yagi–uda antenna with and without a director.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 16. </b><fig><p>Simulated directivity in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">H</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-357-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-357">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane for the modified yagi–uda antenna with and without a director.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Readings at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-358-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-358">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-359-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-359">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for an HT antenna with hybrid directivity could introduce an information data unit because it considers a spacial arrangement of the HT with respect to the reader.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4a4"><h4>4. Theoretical Validation</h4><p>In order to estimate the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-360-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-360">Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula> factor of the distributed matching network included in the HT example, from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a> it is necessary to know <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-361-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-361">R_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{A}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-362-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-362">R_{A}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for each HT. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\rm eq}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-363-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-363">R_{\rm eq}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is obtained by converting the series <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">RC</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-364-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-364">RC</script></tex-math></inline-formula> impedance measured to a shunt <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">RC</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-365-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-365">RC</script></tex-math></inline-formula> equivalent model. Thus, an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{\rm eq}=1.7\ {\hbox{k}}\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-366-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-366">R_{\rm eq}=1.7\ {\hbox{k}}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{\rm eq}=1.03\ {\hbox{pF}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-367-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-367">C_{\rm eq}=1.03\ {\hbox{pF}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is obtained. It is worth noting that after a first prototyping, the capacitive parasitic effects introduced by the chip mounting technique could be added in shunt to the measured capacitance of the chip <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref41" id="context_ref_41_4a4">[41]</a> in order to correct the possible detuning in a further set of prototypes.</p><p>The calculation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{A}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-368-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-368">R_{A}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is not straightforward, given that antenna structures already consider an integrated matching network, its input impedance in a resistive design is unknown. Nevertheless, simulations were carried out in order to approximate the values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{A}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-369-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-369">R_{A}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In the case of the HT example, the simulation mainly considers: 1) a fulfilled conductor for the fundamental resonator of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14(b)</a> avoiding the internal inductive gap effect and 2) a feeding port at the middle of the fundamental resonator. An <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">R_{A}=61.7\ \Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-370-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-370">R_{A}=61.7\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is obtained for the chosen antenna, allowing to calculate a quality factor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q=5.2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-371-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-371">Q=5.2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q^{\ast}=2.1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-372-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-372">Q^{\ast}=2.1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the HT prototype. In agreement to the analysis presented in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2c" class="fulltext-link">Section II-C</a>, the HT example offers a similar treatment to the signals produced by the chip at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-373-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-373">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-374-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-374">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></div></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Prototyping and Testing</h3><p>Once the design meets the desired specifications, several prototypes of the HT example were fabricated using the flip-chip technique for the chip mounting <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref60" id="context_ref_60_4b">[60]</a>. The prototypes are tested with the methods and metrics exposed in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3d" class="fulltext-link">Section III-D</a>, and additionally the fabrication sensitivity is also analyzed. The reported results consider the cases that better illustrate the parameter under evaluation, i.e., fabrication sensitivity, frequency, and power for the designed HT. In order to compare the results with a representative reference, a commercial tag is considered. This tag was selected among nine different samples as the one that better evidences the harmonic backscattering phenomena at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-375-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-375">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> while having good performance at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-376-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-376">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as is shown in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_4b">[27]</a>. It is worth noting that among the nine samples, tags that have even the same kind of chip to the one used in the HT example, described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref61" id="context_ref_61_4b">[61]</a>, did not fit with the selection criteria. The reference tag is hereinafter so-called T5.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4b1"><h4>1. HT Sensitivity At Different Frequencies</h4><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a> shows the measured and estimated sensitivity for the HT in function of the frequency. The estimated values are calculated by post-processing using the simulated scattering parameters of the HT antenna considering the measured chip impedance at 868 MHz and defining an activation threshold for power levels higher than −16 dBm.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>Fabrication sensitivity. From <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a>, a detuning effect of around 12 MHz with respect to 868 MHz is observed. The detuning is mainly caused by the capacitive effect introduced by the flip-chip mounting process. Although detuning is evident, the performance of the HTs is always evaluated at 868 and at 2604 MHz.</p></li><li><p>Bandwidth. In congruence with Yagi–Uda antenna theory, a narrow bandwidth is observed. The simulated bandwidth differs from measurements because the calculated response considers one single point for the chip impedance (at 868 MHz). In all cases, T5 reports the wider bandwidth which according to the theory, it represents the lower <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Q</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-377-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-377">Q</script></tex-math></inline-formula> factor.</p></li></ul>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig17"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-17-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-17-small.gif" alt="Figure 17" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 17. </b><fig><p>Necessary ERP transmitted by the RFID-tp to activate the HT in function of the frequency. The analysis is performed around <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-378-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-378">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and compared to an estimated performance and to the t5 performance.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b2"><h4>2. HT Response At Different RFID-TP Power Levels</h4><p>The HT response in terms of the isotropic received power is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig18" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 18</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">19</a> at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-379-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-379">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-380-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-380">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>Fabrication sensitivity. A direct effect on the activation power is observed and it relies on the antenna-chip impedance matching. The chosen HT antenna structure is sensible to fabrication effects because of the short dimension of the gap between the two parallel lines that carry the feeding point, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a>.</p></li><li><p>Tag response level. In all the cases, the HT presents a response level higher than the response from T5, at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-381-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-381">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-382-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-382">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In the best case, the response of the HT at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-383-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-383">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is 15 dB higher than the one from T5. The 15-dB enhancement relies on both: 1) the choice of a high directivity antenna (6.31 dBi realized directivity) and 2) the harmonic strength generated by the chip represented by the difference <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{15 dB}} -{\hbox{6.3 dBi}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-384-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-384">{\hbox{15 dB}} -{\hbox{6.3 dBi}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></li></ul><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b3"><h4>3. HT Read Range Performance</h4><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig18"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-18-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-18-small.gif" alt="Figure 18" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 18. </b><fig><p>Power of the tag response from HTs at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-385-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-385">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in function of the EIRP transmitted by the RFID-tp at 1 m. The measured power considers an isotropic antenna at reception.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig19"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-19-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-19-small.gif" alt="Figure 19" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 19. </b><fig><p>Power of the tag response from HTs at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-386-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-386">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in function of the EIRP transmitted by the RFID-tp at 1 m. The measured power considers an isotropic antenna at reception.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
The read range performance of the HT is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig20" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 20</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig21" class="fulltext-link">21</a> at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-387-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-387">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-388-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-388">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively.
<ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>Fabrication sensitivity. The manufacturer process introduces an effect on the read range. From <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig20" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 20</a>, as expected, HT tags are very sensible to the fabrication, as shown by the difference of the 2.2-m read range. Similar behavior is observed at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-389-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-389">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig21" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 21</a>.</p></li><li><p>Read range. When simultaneous operation is aimed, the response at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-390-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-390">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> limits the read range of HTs at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-391-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-391">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig21" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 21</a>, greater than 4.5-m read range is achieved if a receiver sensitivity of −90 dBm is attained <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref62" id="context_ref_62_4b3">[62]</a>. In all the cases, the HTs have a higher read range than T5, which under the same criterion, has barely a 2-m read range.</p></li></ul>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig20"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-20-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-20-small.gif" alt="Figure 20" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 20. </b><fig><p>Read range for the the HTs at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-392-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-392">f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in function of 35-dbm EIRP transmitted by the RFID-tp. The measured power considers a 6-dbi antenna at reception.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig21"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-21-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/7234979/7166335/7166335-fig-21-small.gif" alt="Figure 21" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 21. </b><fig><p>Read range for the HTs at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">3f_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-393-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-393">3f_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in function of 35-dbm EIRP transmitted by the RFID-tp. The measured power considers a 6-dbi antenna at reception.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7166335/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion and Perspectives</h2></div><p>A complete theoretical analysis of the harmonics produced by the nonlinear behavior of passive UHF RFID chips has been presented in this paper. The antenna-chip impedance matching is treated with particular attention and design guidelines for new HTs have been exposed. The new HTs are fully compliant with EPC Class-1 Gen2 and exploit the third harmonic generated by the RFID chip to produce a backscatter signal at the third harmonic. This new capability is obtained thanks to a specific design of the matching circuit linking the tag antenna to the RFID chip. Operation concepts for the harmonic communication considering current regulations, harmonic reader, design guidelines for HTs, and evaluation methods have been discussed. The exploitation of the response at the third harmonic by specialized tag antenna design has been experimentally demonstrated. Finally, the evaluation of the prototypes has reported a simultaneous read-range operation at fundamental and third harmonic frequency greater than 4.5 m. Moreover, it has been observed that the HTs show higher sensitivity to the fabrication process due to the significant electrical lengths that the structures exhibits around the third harmonic. Therefore, special care and control of the sources of errors are necessary in the fabrication stage in order to predict the performance by simulation.</p><p>The main contribution of this study is the proof that it is possible to achieve frequency diversity in the EPC Class-1 Gen2 standard context exploiting the modulated third harmonic signal produced by the chip. This approach requires relatively slight modifications of the tags at the cost of increased complexity of the reader that should be able to detect signals at third harmonic frequency. Contrary to the traditional efforts in passive RFID, the nonlinearities are exploited and the objective is not to increase the read range, but to offer a second communication channel from tag-to-reader. It could be noticed that the received third harmonic signal will not be impaired by multi-path and leakage effects at reception as is the case on the fundamental. The authors believe that this new concept could establish a foundation to multiple new applications in the fields of sensing, anti-collision, authentication, or localization. In the field of sensing, the mapping of physical phenomena to harmonics strength and impedance variation at both impedance states can offer more accurate and effective exploitation of backscatter signals. Otherwise it is possible to envisage coarse localization using the zones of illumination by combining antennas at fundamental and harmonic frequencies with different directivity or to exploit the phase information at both frequencies to counter interferences and phase errors caused by strong reflections <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_5">[14]</a>. New algorithms and signal-processing techniques could take advantage of the redundancy and solve collision problems in addition to authenticate one specific tag <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref63" id="context_ref_63_5">[63]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref64" id="context_ref_64_5">[64]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref65" id="context_ref_65_5">[65]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref66" id="context_ref_66_5">[66]</a>. Although not mentioned before, another possible benefit also concerns the field of energy harvesting. Considering the harmonics not as information signals, but energy signals, our first studies demonstrated that it would be possible to recycle the wasted harmonic energy, for instance, in order to empower an embedded sensor or the RFID chip itself to enhance its operation range <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref67" id="context_ref_67_5">[67]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref68" id="context_ref_68_5">[68]</a>. Finally, the exploitation of harmonic signals generated by passive rectifying-based devices, as information carriers, but also as an energy source, establishes the foundations for a wide set of enhancements and new applications, particularly in the field of low-power wireless communication.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGEMENT</h3><p>The authors would like to thank to M. Recouly, Tagsys RFID, for the rich and productive discussions shared and especially for his professional support. A special thanks to the reviewers for their anonymous, voluntary, and extensive assessment of this paper's manuscript; thanks for their valuable comments and suggestions, all of which helped to improve this paper's overall quality.</p></div></div>

He has served as a coordinator and staff member with numerous academic programs, both for education and research. He has served as the Director of ESISAR–Grenoble-INP. He is the founder and past Director of the LCIS Laboratory. He is the founder of the ORSYS group, which he led from 2008 to 2014. <script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

UHF RF identification (RFID) chips. The harmonics generation of passive RFID chips is analyzed to highlight the influences of the matching network and the tag antenna. The proposed study relies on a theoretical model that explains the role in the harmonic production of different elements constituting the tag. The model also shows how to achieve a second communication channel exploiting the third harmonic frequency in addition to the fundamental frequency channel. Specifications and methodology are explained in a harmonic communication scenario. The regulations, harmonic RFID reader considerations, harmonic tag guidelines design, and metrics for its evaluation are discussed.
